Local News

French Minister Wilden Published a Declaration Yesterday

▲ Denying the Franco-Japanese Secret Agreement

▲ And the Invasion of China by French Troops

The French Havas Agency reported on the 19th that French Minister to China Wilden came to Shanghai from Beijing. Recently, due to certain newspapers continuing to publish news of France making military preparations at the border between Vietnam and China, he specially issued the following declaration to the agency in the name of the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Vietnamese government: (1) France and Japan have no secret agreement. (2) No military preparations have been made at the border between Vietnam and China, and no military or civilian aircraft have flown in Chinese airspace. Chinese officials in Longzhou and the Vietnamese government continue to communicate and do not believe in these rumors at all. (3) The director of the Yunnan office in Beijing has already telegraphed General Long Yun, chairman of the Yunnan Provincial Government, and received a reply stating that the French army has not invaded Yunnan, and Yunnan and Vietnam have a good relationship. (4) A certain newspaper claimed that French troops robbed in Gao Bangqiang, but Gao Bangqiang belongs to Vietnam, and I do not understand the robbery. (5) Vietnam has been harassed by the Communist Party, and France will certainly take necessary precautions. These measures are definitely not used to deal with China. Minister Wilden concluded that if France's policy needs to be explained, then the recent meeting of the League of Nations Executive Council should be explained. For the past two months, French Foreign Minister Briand has made great efforts to help resolve the Sino-Japanese dispute, which no one can deny. And no one can deny his tireless efforts for the cause of peace, so that the peaceful situation can continue to be maintained.

Guangdong Committee Will Arrive Tomorrow Morning

▲ Tan Zhen, Li Liejun, and others Will Enter Beijing First This Morning

The 19 members of the Guangdong Committee, including Chen Jitang, Huang Shaoxiong, and Ma Chaojun, arrived in Shanghai on the Changxing Company's Russian Empress ship from Hong Kong the day before yesterday. It was originally scheduled to arrive here at about 5:00 PM today, but due to the fog at sea yesterday, the ship was delayed and could not arrive as scheduled. According to the company, it will probably be delayed until about 8:00 AM tomorrow morning before it can arrive here. At that time, the company will specially prepare small steamships to travel between Pudong and the Xinguankoutou to pick up and drop off passengers. It is estimated that Chen and others will take the company's small steamship to cross the river and land at the Xinguankoutou. It is also heard that after Chen and others arrive in Shanghai, they will rest briefly and then take the Jinghu afternoon train or night train together to Beijing to attend the meeting. As for the eight members of the Central Committee in Shanghai, Tan Zhen, Li Liejun, Cheng Qian, Fang Zhenwu, Xiong Kewu, Zhang Zhiben, Fu Rulin, and Chen Jiayou, they originally intended to wait for Chen Jitang and others to arrive in Shanghai today before going to Beijing together. However, due to the postponement of Chen and others' arrival in Shanghai and the opening date of the First Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Committee already reaching, they decided to take the Jinghu early train at 9:30 AM today and go to Beijing first to attend the meeting.

Pan Gongzhan Talks About Party Affairs, Commercial and Industrial Disputes

▲ Party Affairs Must Wait for Central Resolution

▲ Chamber of Commerce Presented to the Municipal Government for Handling

▲ The General Labor Union Has No Legal Basis

The China News Agency reported that disputes between party affairs, the Chamber of Commerce, the Labor Union, and various groups have been recurring in this city recently. A reporter from the China News Agency visited Mr. Pan Gongzhan at the Social Affairs Bureau at 3:00 PM yesterday and asked for his views. He answered as follows:

▲ Party Affairs Issues The executive and supervisory committee members of the Municipal Party Department are all elected by party members throughout the city and have been approved by the Central Committee. Therefore, they were produced in accordance with the law. Although there has been a general resignation, their mission has not ended before the Central Committee has expressly approved it. Therefore, the work will naturally continue as usual. As for the so-called improvement committee and other organizations, the party constitution has no regulations, and they are not elected by party members throughout the city or appointed by the Central Committee. Therefore, although the current Municipal Party Department committee members are eager to resign to reduce their responsibilities, they will definitely not be able to hand over to any illegally produced organization. As for the improvement committee issue, the Municipal Party Department has submitted a request to the Central Committee for resolution.

▲ Chamber of Commerce Issues National peace and social order depend on the maintenance of the law. The Social Affairs Bureau has always relied on the law to resolve any incident. The establishment of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce was established in accordance with the law. It naturally exists before it is formally reorganized in accordance with the law. Yesterday, the so-called Commercial Movement Committee went to take over. The Social Affairs Bureau did not know about this matter in advance. We do not know what the basis of the association is. As for what happened yesterday, we have already sent people to investigate and have submitted a report to the Municipal Government. How to resolve it in the future will be handled by the Municipal Government.

▲ Labor Union Issues Upon investigation, the People's Organization Law and the Labor Union Law promulgated by the Central Committee do not have an organizational law for the General Labor Union. Before the Central Committee promulgates a new organizational law, there is naturally no need to organize the General Labor Union. Moreover, the establishment of people's organizations has always required the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau to send people to guide them. The fact that there are two places organizing the General Labor Union today, I do not know about.

Ma Zhanshan's Two Replies

▲ Reply to the Life Weekly Agency's Telegram The Life Weekly Agency previously telegraphed General Ma to inquire about whether there was a proper way to extract the remittance, to avoid fraudulent receipt, in order to ensure the safe delivery of the donation to General Ma. Now it is learned that the agency has received a reply telegram from General Ma from Hailun, stating that the telegram from the Life Weekly Agency has been respectfully received. All funds entrusted to your agency by various parties can be extracted by the commissioner of our office in Harbin with my official seal, so that it will not be fraudulently received. Please remit the funds to us. In addition to the successive remittances, we will report to you after we have collected all of them. Sincerely, Ma Zhanshan (seal)." It is also learned that as of the 18th, the agency has received a total of 105,934 yuan and 45 cents in donations to General Wei Zhanshan. Except for the 55,507 yuan that has been remitted to General Ma and received, the rest are being remitted.

▲ Reply to the Lida Academy's Telegram The teachers and students of the Shanghai Jiangwan Lida Academy previously entrusted the Bank of China to remit 400 yuan to General Ma Zhanshan on the 10th of this month. It is learned that the academy has received a reply telegram from General Ma, stating that the telegram from the Shanghai Jiangwan Lida Academy has been respectfully received. Thank you for your encouragement and generous donation. I hereby express my sincere gratitude to my troops. Our government has now moved to Hailun, and the funds have been sent to Harbin to be transferred. Sincerely, Ma Zhanshan (seal).

▲ Arriving in Shanghai on the Nagasaki Maru on the 23rd

According to local diplomatic sources, the National Government has specially telegraphed Minister to Japan Jiang Zuobin to return to China to inquire about everything related to Sino-Japanese diplomacy. After receiving the order, Jiang left Tokyo for Kobe yesterday and is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the Nagasaki Maru on the 23rd of this month, and then go to Beijing to report and attend the First Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Committee. It is also said that Jiang will be assigned another position after being summoned back to China, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs plans to send a special diplomatic talent to Japan.

The Jinpu Railway passenger and freight trains, which were previously blocked by students petitioning to go to Beijing, resumed normal operations for both north- and south-bound trains at approximately 5:00 PM yesterday.

Japanese Fleet and Disarmament Representatives

▲ Both Arrive and Depart This Morning

▲ Training Ships Return Home The Japanese Navy training fleet, consisting of the Asama and Iwate, carrying 170 naval students and over 1,430 officers and sailors, arrived in Shanghai from locations including Korea, Dalian, and Qingdao. Over the past few days, Japanese officials and civilians in Shanghai have hosted the officers and students, and the soldiers and cadets have also gone ashore for sightseeing. As of last night, the allotted time for their visit to Shanghai had expired. All soldiers and students have returned to their ships, and the two ships, under the command of Commander Imamura, are scheduled to depart Shanghai at 6:30 AM this morning, heading directly back to the Sasebo naval port in Japan.

▲ Delegation Arrives in Shanghai The Japanese delegation to the League of Nations Disarmament Conference, appointed by the Japanese government, consists of Army Lieutenant General Matsui Iwane as plenipotentiary representative, along with 21 staff members including Maruyama Juntaro, as well as Navy Vice Admiral Nagano Osami as plenipotentiary representative, along with 22 staff members including Kohata Kazusuke, and Kato Denjiro (an official of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs), representing the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, making a total of 49 members. They have traveled to Europe aboard the Japanese postal ship Suwa Maru. The ship is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai tomorrow morning. Ambassador Shigemitsu and others stationed in Shanghai are preparing to welcome them. The delegation will stay in Shanghai for one day and then continue to Marseille on the same ship.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Repays Old Debt Public Bonds

▲ Available for Collection from January 4th Next Year Upon Presentation of Bonds

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, in order to repay the principal and interest of the construction public bonds of the former General Chamber of Commerce and the South Shanghai Chamber of Commerce starting from January 4th of the twenty-first year of the Republic, issued an announcement yesterday, which is detailed below:

▲ First Announcement Regarding the Repayment of Principal and Interest of Construction Public Bonds of the Former General Chamber of Commerce states: The former Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, in order to build a meeting hall and a product exhibition hall, issued the first and second rounds of construction public bonds. The original plan at the time specified that the additional 30% membership fee collected would be used as collateral. Each installment of principal and interest was repaid according to the plan. However, since the seventeenth year of the Republic, the former Shanghai Special Municipality General Chamber of Commerce claimed that the membership fees were insufficient, and the principal and interest payments were temporarily suspended. The outstanding amount includes one installment (the twelfth) from the first round and three installments (the tenth to the twelfth) from the second round. After the establishment of this Chamber of Commerce, all additional 30% membership fees collected have been specifically earmarked and strictly prohibited from being misappropriated. It is estimated that by the end of this year, all the additional membership fees collected will be sufficient to repay the above four installments of principal and interest. Therefore, at the second members' meeting in July of this year, it was already resolved that repayment would begin in January of the twenty-first year of the Republic. A special announcement is hereby made in accordance with the plan. Bondholders can go to the Finance Department of this Chamber of Commerce to collect the principal and interest upon presentation of the bonds, starting from January 4th next year, every day from 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM, except for Sundays and other public holidays. As for the reorganization public bonds raised by the former General Chamber of Commerce in the fourteenth year of the Republic, after the current construction public bonds are repaid, the additional 30% membership fees collected from the twenty-first year of the Republic can be transferred as collateral for this item of principal and interest. A separate notice will be issued after a plan is devised.

▲ Second Announcement Regarding the Repayment of Construction Public Bonds of the Former South Shanghai Chamber of Commerce states: The former South Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, in order to build a meeting hall, issued public bonds, originally designating the rental income from the Chamber's property as collateral. The principal and interest were paid up to the fourth installment. After the takeover by the former Merchant Organizations Reorganization Committee, it was further resolved that the rental income from the Chamber's meeting hall, which was rented to the Social Affairs Bureau, would be stored together for the purpose of allocating it to repay the principal and interest of these public bonds. This Chamber of Commerce was established and continued to handle this matter. It is estimated that by the end of this year, this rental income will be sufficient to repay the principal and interest of the fifth installment. Therefore, at the second members' meeting in July of this year, it was resolved that repayment would begin in January of the twenty-first year of the Republic. A special announcement is hereby made in accordance with the plan. Holders of bonds for the fifth installment of the construction public bonds of the former South Shanghai Chamber of Commerce can go to the Finance Department of this Chamber of Commerce to collect the principal and interest upon presentation of the bonds, starting from January 4th of the twenty-first year of the Republic, every day from 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM, except for Sundays and public holidays. This announcement is hereby made.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Assists in Collecting and Paying Business Tax

▲ Office Issued a Notice Yesterday

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce's Office for Assisting in the Collection and Payment of Business Tax issued Notice No. 1 yesterday, stating: For the purpose of notification, the implementation of business tax in this city is imminent. The Municipal Finance Bureau has entrusted the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to handle the collection matters and has assigned members of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to organize this office to specially handle this matter. The first step is for the businesses to fill out a business operator declaration form so that the government can compile a tax collection roster and collect taxes on a regular basis. The Finance Bureau has already announced an extension for the declaration form and reminded that penalties will be imposed for violations. The extension period is about to expire, but shops in various industries have not yet completely filled out the forms, which is a delay. Therefore, personnel are specially dispatched to urge compliance. It is hoped that attention will be paid to the following key points and that the forms will be filled out and submitted as soon as possible to avoid penalties by the government. This announcement is hereby made. The details are as follows: (1) All shops in various industries that have already established industry associations, regardless of whether they have joined the association as members, should directly obtain the forms from the association, fill them out, and then submit them to the association for forwarding. (2) Shops in various industries that do not yet have an industry association should directly obtain the forms from this office (inside the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at Tianhou Palace Bridge), fill them out, and then submit them to this office. (3) If shops in various industries have any unclear points regarding the declaration procedures, they can ask the personnel who come to them for clarification. They will be informed clearly. If the personnel have any questions regarding the scope of the business tax, please also inform them as much as possible to avoid misunderstandings.

Five District Branches' Propositions on Party Affairs

The Second, Fifth, Sixth, Ninth, and Tenth District Branches of the Shanghai Special Municipality of the Chinese Kuomintang jointly telegraphed: To party headquarters at all levels, all organizations, and all newspapers, Since Comrade Chiang Kai-shek resigned, there has been hope for reform in both party affairs and politics. Examining past facts, we believe that the goals of improvement should be as follows: The corruption of party affairs in the past was due to the loss of the spirit of democracy. Party members did not have the right to free elections, resulting in a few people being able to manipulate and control them through bribery and coercion, forming a phenomenon of a minority suppressing the majority. In the future, party affairs must first abolish the system of pre-selected candidates to restore the electoral rights of party members so that party members have a deeper relationship with the party. Secondly, all issues within the party must be discussed openly, with the minority submitting to the majority. In this way, the spirit of democracy can be realized. The current political focus should be on diplomacy. However, internal unity must precede external unity. Comrades in our party should unite as one in the future. The people of the whole country must also unite as one, and only then will we have strength externally. In diplomatic matters, we advocate adhering to the principles of no withdrawal of troops and no negotiations, and we oppose the signing of any conditions that harm our rights. Before clarifying the intention, we also oppose the arrival of international investigation teams in China. In domestic affairs, we support the convening of a national crisis conference or a national salvation conference to allow the people to participate in the government and seek the realization of national unity against foreign aggression, guiding political tutelage on the path to constitutionalism. In the past, mass movements were inactive. Now that the diplomatic situation is urgent, the strength of the masses is the only force against foreign aggression and must be restored, which has already been restored in practice. However, in the labor movement, there must be an organization of the General Labor Union. The distinction between industry and commerce should not be based on the nature of the organization served but on whether it is employed. Therefore, shop clerks should have an organization of trade unions or shop clerks' unions and should not join trade associations. The right to strike for workers must be recognized because past mediation and arbitration could not restrict the employer's freedom to dismiss or close factories. Workers have no means of self-defense. Student movements were not recognized in the past as having the right to organize student unions. They could not only not participate in political movements, but they could not also interfere in school administration. They had organizations in name only, without any function. The current Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association is a temporary organization used to resist foreign aggression. In the future, the organization of student unions and student federations must be restored. In addition to participating in political movements, their functions should also seek the welfare of students to curb the school authorities from exploiting students under various names to achieve their profit-making goals of commercialized education. In the merchant movement, there is nothing seriously wrong with the current trade associations and chambers of commerce. However, the distinctions of the trade associations are unlimited and have become a disguised form of the guildhall. This should be improved. Moreover, the restrictions on the union of local trade associations or chambers of commerce are too strict and should not exist. Other organizations of self-employed professionals and cultural and social organizations should not have restrictions of one organization per locality. An absolute principle of free organization should be adopted. There are many corrupt elements in the municipal party headquarters, and facts of corruption are often exposed to society, causing laughter both domestically and abroad. Recently, the handling of mass movements has been extremely inappropriate. We also sympathize with the principle of reorganization, but the reorganization must comply with the general charter and the agreement of the majority. If a few people establish various names separately or carry out the organization through the speculative means of transformation by the original members, we are absolutely opposed. All of the above are the results of our collective discussion and are defined as the goals of our struggle in the future. Anyone willing to join forces in common effort is welcome. The current communication address is temporarily set up at No. B426, Route Lafayette, French Concession, to facilitate contact with all parties. The telegram is urgent. We await your clear instructions.

Important Shipping News

▲ Towing the Ruiyang The Nisshin Kisen's public Yangtze River steamer Ruiyang Maru ran aground on the Wushang Sandbar upstream of Tongzhou, damaging the hull. This was previously reported. It has now been learned that after securing the hull with large timbers, the Nisshin Kisen has decided to send Chief Captain Takeshita to Wushang Sandbar tomorrow to arrange for towing. Workers and towing equipment will also be taken along. It is planned to tow the ship back to Shanghai and then enter the shipyard for major repairs.

▲ Progress of Chinese Ships Since the boycott of Japanese ships, the business of British ships in Shanghai has been very prosperous. Chinese merchant ships have been released back to Shanghai by the headquarters, and after restoring scheduled services, cargo and passengers have become even more crowded. Various shipping companies have all made profits. Last month, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's business, after expenses, had a surplus of more than 100,000 taels. After adding new ships this month, the income from freight will be even greater, and the surplus will be even more. In recent days, Guo Waifeng has convened meetings of the heads of various departments to discuss issues such as the bureau's affairs, operations, and economics. The agenda of the meeting is kept secret.

▲ Hong Kong Price Increase The various shipping companies in Shanghai have agreed that, starting from the 15th of this month, the freight rate for goods shipped from Shanghai to Hong Kong will be increased by 10% across the board according to the set rate. All customers have been notified to take note.

Weihaiwei Radio Station to Begin Trial Reporting Today

The International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications has added a radio station in Weihaiwei. Since its preparation, it has been nearly four months. Initially, the site leased in that port was insufficient for application. Since changing the location, the radio station has been installed. Recently, the preparations have been completed, and it has been decided to implement trial reporting today (the 20th). It has also been planned to communicate with the Shanghai, Nanjing, Qingdao, and Jinan areas for trial reporting. The radio station in that port has both longwave and shortwave installations. When the shortwave is officially reported, it will only communicate with the above four ports. However, reporting with various parts of the country will depend on the location, and the four ports will forward the shortwave radio stations. It is the coastal ship reporting service, and the official reporting will be done by the bureau selecting a date and notifying Weihaiwei to handle it. It is said that the date is not far away, at the latest within ten days.

Wang Songfa, Who Robbed and Killed Three People, Sentenced to Death

▲ Wang Smiled Carelessly After Hearing the Verdict

▲ Asked by What Method He Would Be Executed

Wang Jiasun, a native of Ningbo, owner of the Wang Yuanxing sawmill at No. 1673, East Xihua Road, his wife Zhang, and Yu Xingbao, were murdered at approximately 1:00 AM on the 5th of this month while they were sound asleep in the front building. Wang Songfa, his grand-nephew, planned the crime out of resentment and greed, using a kitchen knife to kill all three of them, stealing 130 silver dollars and a deposit book for the Shanghai Siming Bank with a total of 1,781 yuan, and fleeing to the home of his friend Xie Jinbao in Zhoushanbang, Wuxi. Later, because the stolen money was running out, he falsely told Xie that his grandfather, Wang Jiasun, had passed away and that he had secretly taken a Siming deposit book and asked him to go to Shanghai to collect the money on his behalf. Xie, unaware of the situation and illiterate, accompanied his friend Feng Song to Shanghai to collect the money from the bank, and the case was exposed. Xie Shuiquan, a Chinese detective of the Huishan Police Station, and detectives Qi Mengqing and Liu Baoshan successively arrested them and went to Wuxi to arrest Wang Songfa. The police determined that Feng Song was indeed a legitimate businessman who was temporarily deceived and specially declared to the First Special District Court for preliminary release. Xie Jinbao and Wang Songfa were interrogated by Judge Shen Bingrong on various aspects of the case and were awaiting sentencing. The details have been published in this newspaper. Yesterday morning was the date of the verdict. The police escorted Wang Songfa and related person Xie Jinbao to the First High Court. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, stated that Xie Jinbao should be released. Wang Jinfeng, the young daughter of the victim, also came to court, saying that the Siming Bank deposit book had been issued by the previous court, but the money had not yet been received. Judge Shen then ruled that Wang Songfa was sentenced to death for premeditated murder, sentenced to death for two counts of murder, and sentenced to one year of imprisonment for theft, all to be carried out by execution. Wang Songfa smiled carelessly after hearing the verdict, saying, "The court sentenced me to death. What method will be used to execute me?" Judge Shen said, "You will know when it is carried out." Xie Jinbao was immediately released, and he declared to the young Wang Jinfeng that the bank deposit would be notified to the bank again to be issued.

Li Quanlin, Who Murdered and Robbed, Executed by Firing Squad

▲ The First Death Sentence Judged by the Second Special District Court

▲ His Attitude Was Extremely Terrified Before the Execution

Li Quanlin, a criminal sentenced to death by the Second Special District Court after the French Concession Public Court was taken back, was a native of Wujin. His case involved colluding with Yuan Changsheng and others to rob in the vicinity of Minguo Road and Nanyang Bridge, as well as robbing the Changxing Tobacco and Paper Shop at No. 91 Lanwei Ail Road, and shooting and killing shop employee Gao Ronghua. The French police Chinese detective caught him with a target in the Luoshenfu Road, searched for a pistol and bullets, and escorted him to the Second Special Court. Judge Ge interrogated Li, who confessed without denying, so he was sentenced to death. A petition was submitted to the provincial government for a reply telegram, ordering him to be sent to the Chinese-administered district court for execution. Yesterday morning, the executing judge opened the court and brought Li to the case for identity verification. He was then escorted to the execution ground of the No. 2 Prison in Caohejing by bailiffs and others. Wang Sixian, a prosecutor appointed by the District Court, served as the execution supervisor, along with Secretary Yu, Examiner Shen, etc., and ordered Police Chief Xu Jinqing, Police Officer Chen Xihui, and Supervising Execution Police Xue Bingzhang, Gu Hanqing, Yin Daoxu, Zhu Wanyuan, and Zhang Chunsen, etc., to go to the execution ground. After the judge and Warden Dong took their seats, Li was brought to the case and stated that he was 33 years old, his wife was a wet nurse in Dr. Zhang Long's house on Pingqiao Road, and his father was already 66 years old. He asked to buy a coffin to collect his body, etc. His attitude was extremely terrified, and he could not move. The judge ordered the execution. Police Chief Xu directed the bailiffs to take him down for execution by firing squad.

Young Man Commits Suicide in Inn

▲ Signed as Zhang Jianxun, Native of Jiangxi, 31 Years Old

▲ Used a Knife to Stab His Throat, His Life Is Feared to Be In Danger

At around 4:30 PM yesterday afternoon, a young man dressed in a royal blue Western suit with a thin and long face suddenly arrived at the Andong Inn on Daxin Street, No. 66 Hubei Road. The traveler was carrying a small wicker basket in his right hand and an umbrella in his left arm. He signed his name as Zhang Jianxun, 31 years old, a native of Jiangxi, and a member of the academic community. The inn's accountant led him to room No. 241 on the second floor, agreeing on a daily room rate of 2.86 yuan. The young man first paid 3 silver dollars. At around 9:00 PM that night, the young man took off his coat, leaving only a shirt, and ordered a bowl of winter mushroom noodles from the waiter. After eating, he closed the door tightly, as if going to bed. However, there was a piece of glass in room No. 241, which faced the waiter's counter. One of the waiters suddenly caught a glimpse of fresh red bloodstains on the bed curtain in room No. 241. The waiter was shocked and rushed to open the door. He only saw the young man lying on the bed, with blood flowing profusely from his throat. His right hand was still holding a razor, and a pointed Western knife was also placed beside the bed. It was determined to be a suicide. He immediately reported it to the Laozha Police Station, which dispatched detectives to investigate carefully. He had not yet died, and he was immediately taken to Tongren Hospital. However, the wound was very deep, and his life was feared to be in danger.

Refugee Relief Centers Continuously Repatriate Large Numbers of Refugees

▲ Gaoyou Fellow-Countrymen Association Asks to Continue Accepting Them

▲ Refugee Relief Committee The Shanghai Refugee Relief Committee held its fourth regular meeting at 5:00 PM yesterday afternoon. Qu Wenliu, Hu Hongji (representing Shen Hao), Lu Bohong, Li Yunshu, Wang Binyan, Pan Gongzhan, Feng Liutang, Huang Hanzhi, Lu Shaoze, Gu Junyang, Zhu Qiluo, Wang Yiting, and others attended. Wang Yiting was elected as chairman. The agenda was as follows: (1) Report on the repatriation and relief situation for this week, (2) A case of Gengji Shelter's request for an additional five yuan per square for the refugee shelter sheds it built was resolved by approving an additional one yuan per square, (3) Report on the outline of income and expenditure accounts for this week, (4) The Gaoyou Fellow-Countrymen Association sent a letter stating that refugee representatives and others requested a temporary postponement of repatriation to their original places of origin. It was resolved to reply to the association that the repatriation of refugees by the committee was a form of financial assistance, and since the original places of origin were also handling winter relief after their return, there would definitely not be any starvation.

▲ Repatriation of Large Numbers of Refugees The Shanghai Refugee Relief Center, due to the large number of refugees arriving in Shanghai in recent days, has been financially assisting refugees for repatriation every day since the 16th of this month. On the 16th, 139 refugees were transported by the Datong Company's Zida Ship to Huojiaqiao, Yangzhou. On the 17th, 295 refugees were transported by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jianghua Ship to Hankou, Anhui, Wuhu, and Changsha. On the 18th, 201 refugees were transported by the Dada Company's Daqing Ship to Huojiaqiao. On the 19th, 588 refugees were transported by the Sanbei Company's Changan Ship to Hankou. It is reported that all the companies have waived the fares and only charged for food, which is half a yuan per person for those below Zhenjiang and one and a half yuan per person for Anqing and Hankou.

▲ Letter from the Gaoyou Fellow-Countrymen Association The Shanghai Gaoyou Fellow-Countrymen Association sent a letter to the Shanghai Refugee Relief Committee, stating: Recently, the refugees Jin Liunan, Zhang Diaobin, and others from the First Refugee Relief Center came to the association and claimed that the refugee relief center is now carrying out the second repatriation. The refugees have no homes to return to and are waiting for death. They are specially reporting this to request assistance. Their voices were tearful, and their situation is truly pitiful. In general, refugees from various places have come here to escape death and seek survival. At this time of severe winter, suddenly repatriating them to their clothing- and food-less hometowns will inevitably lead to nine deaths out of ten, which is no different from driving them into ditches. Moreover, at a time when the country is in great difficulty, taking risks is especially worrying. We still hope that your committee will embrace benevolence, continue to maintain them, and wait until the warm spring to repatriate them to their original places of origin to engage in spring plowing. This will be a thorough rescue of people and will not lose the committee's original charitable intention. We are now recommending that Mr. Yang Kunyue of our association go to see you in person to plead with you. Please immediately grant our request. If you approve, not only will thousands of refugees express their gratitude in unison, but our association will also represent them in bowing nine times to thank you.

Plumber's License Should Be Submitted to the Public Works Bureau for Inspection

▲ Next January is the License Verification Deadline

The Municipal Public Works Bureau registers plumbers and apprentices in the city, issuing each person a license to work. According to regulations, these licenses must be submitted to the bureau for inspection once every year in January. It is now learned that the bureau has sent letters to various plumbing shops, instructing the employed plumbers and apprentices to bring their licenses and fees (one yuan for plumbers, fifty cents for apprentices) to the bureau for processing within the deadline. Failure to verify the licenses within the deadline will result in penalties in accordance with regulations.

Judgment in the Yi Xin Li Housing Lawsuit

▲ Tenants Hosted Various Sectors Last Night

▲ It Was Decided on the Spot to Form a Support Association

The houses in the Yi Xin Li area belong to wealthy merchants Cheng Linsheng and Cheng Yize. Recently, the Chengs ordered all tenants to vacate the houses, but the tenants refused, leading to a lawsuit. The Special First District Court has summoned the parties multiple times and concluded the case, as previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the judgment in this case. The plaintiff's lawyer, Wang Youling, the lawyer for the joined party, Wang Fuchang of the Public Interest and Philanthropic Association, and the defendant's lawyer, Wang Chuanbi, all appeared in court. At 2:30 PM, Judge He Qi ascended the bench in the Civil Division 9 and announced the judgment. The main text of the judgment stated: "The defendants, Taichang Woodware Store and fifteen other businesses, must vacate the houses, and provisional execution is permitted. Rongchangxiang must vacate by March 6, 1932, and provisional execution is permitted. The litigation costs are to be borne by the defendants." Furthermore, the China Photo Studio and Rongchangxiang Western Clothing Store, representing the Yi Xin Li tenants' association, hosted various sectors at the Atlantic Restaurant last night to appeal against the forced eviction. They further stated that the provisional execution judged by the Special District Court yesterday was urgent, and they urgently sought a solution. Hundreds of representatives from various sectors attended the reception last night, and it was decided on the spot to form a support committee to proceed with the matter.

The Jardine Matheson & Co. Sues Shen Chengfu Case

▲ One Matter, Two Lawsuits, Redundant Structure

▲ The Repayment Issue Still Needs to Be Discussed

The British firm Jardine Matheson & Co. filed a lawsuit because the bills of exchange of more than 500,000 yuan paid by its cotton compradore Shen Chengfu were due, and the Zhichang Qianzhuang, which issued the bills, had gone bankrupt and could not be cashed. At that time, Shen Chengfu also abandoned his job and fled. The foreign firm then filed a lawsuit against Shen in the First Special District Court for payment.

Subsequently, it accused Shen of embezzlement in the Criminal Division of the court and also attached a civil lawsuit. The defendant has now been detained. The foreign firm's one matter, two lawsuits is truly a redundant structure. When Judge Guo Shouyi of the Farmer's Division heard the case yesterday, he made many corrections to the plaintiff's prosecution procedure. The general idea was that since the plaintiff had already filed an independent lawsuit regarding the due and uncashable bills of exchange, it should wait for the Civil Division to hear the case. However, in the embezzlement case, there was also an attached civil lawsuit. However, since this case was filed first, it is not subject to another case, and so on. Subsequently, the lawyers for both parties debated, and the defendant Shen Chengfu completely acknowledged the bills of exchange. Since the two sides still needed to discuss the issue of repayment, Judge Guo adjourned the case to the 26th of this month for further review.

Bao Ziming is Actually Cai Fei

▲ Transferred to Headquarters Yesterday

Bao Ziming, a native of Tongzhou, is 31 years old. He was previously involved in a gang kidnapping case in the French Concession. He was arrested by the French police and sent to the former Public Concession, where he was sentenced to imprisonment after interrogation. Now, the Shanghai Garrison Headquarters has learned that the criminal Bao is actually Cai Fei, the leader of the Communist bandits. Therefore, it specifically sent a document to the Second Special District Court, requesting permission to transfer him for interrogation. Yesterday morning, the court sent police to the prison to bring the criminal Bao to the First Court. Judge Zhang Shijie interrogated him, and Yang Fengqi, the inspector of the detective team sent by the headquarters, arrived to transfer him. After Judge Zhang briefly interrogated the defendant, he ordered that Bao Ziming be handed over to the officers from the headquarters to be taken away for interrogation.

Young Woman Addicted to Gambling on Flower Associations Results in

▲ Suicide by Poisoning

Zhang Sun, a young woman from Wuxi, was 27 years old and lived at No. 110 Jiangyin Back Street, Xiaosimeng, Nanshi. Her husband, Rong Da, was a leather business man and a opium addict. Because it was inconvenient to smoke opium in the Chinese territory, he rented a pavilion room on the upper floor of the Xiangji Barber Shop at No. 55 Yushun Lane, Dongxin Street, French Concession, as a den. She also went there every afternoon to play and did not return to Nanshi with him until late at night. This became a habit, but she was addicted to flower associations and lost repeatedly, eventually pawning all her jewelry and clothes. Yesterday, her husband scolded her slightly. Afterwards, she became extremely depressed and suddenly had the idea of dying. She took a large amount of Resorcinol and soon became poisoned and beyond rescue. Her husband noticed and took her to Renji Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. She died at around 7 o'clock. Many pawn tickets were found in her pocket, a considerable number. The deceased was wearing red and black floral silk material, an old sheepskin cheongsam, a cropped haircut, and leather shoes. Her dress was still modern. Subsequently, the hospital notified the Da Zi Ming Zhong police station, and investigator Wang Licheng went to investigate. Then, the body was transported for an autopsy pending the autopsy.

Reader's Letter

Opinions on the Student Demonstration Group's Questioning of the Guangdong Committee - Zhang Wuntian

Seeing the "Domestic Important News" column of Shen Bao, which carries "Student demonstration groups telegraphing to Wang [Jingwei] to transfer to the Guangdong side committee, asking whether the new National Government authorities can declare war on Japan, can recover lost territory, can withdraw from the League of Nations, can punish Zhang Xueliang, if not, then like the original rulers, don't blame the anti-Japanese masses for treating you the same..." I couldn't help but itch to say a few words. Before speaking, I want to state that I am not a student, nor a member of any party, nor a pawn of any organization or individual. I am completely an ordinary citizen speaking from the standpoint of jointly facing the national crisis. No one can deny the mistakes of the previous authorities in handling national affairs. In the past few days, the situation has taken a sharp turn, and the new authorities have been replaced. Whether they can, as we fervently hope and as they have stated, save the precarious China, whether they can do it, cannot be predicted now. We should actively offer opinions to the new authorities, and criticize and supervise them. At the same time, we must encourage the courage of the new authorities, hold on to the original propositions, and fight to the end without any hesitation. We should not come and give them a blow to the head, making them discouraged. The wording of the student demonstration group's telegram completely loses the above-mentioned spirit and attitude, which cannot but make us suspicious under ardent sympathy. First, in China's current situation and environment, and the general level of political life of the masses, the domestic and foreign propositions now stated by the new authorities are needed. Whether they can be implemented will naturally be questioned in the future. The tone of the student demonstration group seems to have an attitude of distrust. This distrust is due to the propositions of the new authorities, or the individual members of the new authorities, is not known. If it is said to be a proposition, then the foreign propositions are no different from those of the demonstration group, and the demonstration group has not seen any other propositions for the domestic situation. If it is said to be due to the individual members of the new authorities, then why not point them out? Second, the central issue of anti-Japanese resistance is how to recover lost territory without harming national interests. The issues of declaring war on Japan, withdrawing from the League of Nations, and punishing Zhang Xueliang (I propose that this should be decided after the Northeast Incident comes to an end) all revolve around this issue. As for whether the new authorities can recover the lost territory, it is determined by whether the new authorities and the national masses can work together in the future. At this moment, no omnipotent government or individual can have a definite answer, unless you ask them whether they have the determination to recover the lost territory. Third, seeking the victory of anti-Japanese resistance must seek the human track of internal affairs. This principle is certainly true, but anti-Japanese efforts cannot be weakened because of domestic issues. At present, most of the actions of the general students belong to the domestic affairs. For the recovery of lost territory and the declaration of war on Japan, I have not seen any practical and painstaking preparation work. It is as if the huge anti-Japanese work is entirely the responsibility of the government, and nothing needs to be done without a virtuous government. This concept is a big mistake. To be honest, we are relatively implicit in the current changes in the situation. Whether it is reliable in the future is not yet to be discussed. At present, we should, on the one hand, do some preparations for the recovery of lost territory very hard, very practically, and with a plan, and on the other hand, encourage the courage of the new authorities, hold on to the original propositions, and fight to the end, and at the same time, add strict criticism and supervision. We should not passively question, blame, or even threaten turmoil. In the past few years, the political disturbances in the country have made the general masses and young students sink to a terrible level. This time, due to the crisis of the national foundation, the phenomenon of gradual activity is truly valuable. It is also a mistake not to add encouragement and supervision to this valuable active situation of the Chinese people. I have seen the actions and words of students and demonstration groups in the past few days, and they often deviate from the original intention of resisting Japan and saving the country, so I have these words. I hope that the student demonstration group will work hard and move forward based on its original intention, and do not mess up the pace or lose the sympathy of students across the country and the general public. At the same time, I hope that the new government authorities can implement the original propositions and accept the opinions, criticisms, and supervision of the people. The patience and ardent hopes of the people are all in this move, and only in this move. The time is not to be missed again.

(Reply) It is too early to criticize the new authorities now, or to trust the new authorities now. This matter all depends on whether the new authorities can immediately announce a few fundamental facilities to show the people a new beginning when they first come to power. Threatening turmoil is certainly not appropriate, but reasonable questioning and blame are also a kind of supervisory role. If the new authorities sincerely want to comfort the people's aspirations, they can answer frankly because of their questioning.

Letters to the Editor

Respectfully, I have just read in your esteemed newspaper of December 19th a telegram from Zhang Zhijiang to Chen Jitang, which I find most surprising. Upon investigation, Jiang and Mr. Chen have never had any official superior-subordinate relationship. The form of address in the telegram is completely inappropriate and clearly a fabrication. I am therefore writing to request that you publish a correction. Your assistance in this matter would be greatly appreciated. Respectfully, Zhang Zhijiang, to the Chief Editor of Shen Bao.

Esteemed Editor, regarding the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau's exhibition of achievements in patriotic activities of primary and secondary schools, upon receiving the Bureau's notice, our school actively prepared for registration, completed the report forms, and completed all procedures according to the Bureau's stipulated date. On the afternoon of the 11th (the day before the exhibition), at 2:00 PM, we sent personnel to Wu Ben Middle School (as the newspaper reported that the first venue was Wu Ben, and our school was listed in the first venue), to report to the preparatory committee office and inquire about the display location. The first reply from Director Zhong stated that it was on the second floor of the new building, number two. Unexpectedly, number two belonged to Guang Zhao Middle School. At that time, our school thought that Mr. Zhong was mistaken, so we returned to the office to explain the school name. Mr. Zhong searched through the papers he held, but said there was no name of our school, and that our school's registration procedures were incorrect. Our school repeatedly explained that the registration procedures were definitely not wrong, and that the newspaper and the signs posted outside the venue also had the name of our school, which could prove it. However, Mr. Zhong still did not acknowledge that our school was registered. After our school's repeated statements, Mr. Zhong pointed to the two playgrounds as display rooms. At the same time, several schools had already displayed their materials in the two playgrounds, and our school had many charts and graphs, which were insufficient in space. After much negotiation, Mr. Shao then led us to the girls' embroidery room of the school. Our school prepared to display, but unexpectedly, the school authorities said that this place was not designated for display and could not be approved. So our school could not display again. We contacted Mr. Zhong again, and Mr. Zhong kept saying "wait a little, wait a little, there will be a solution." But that day was the anniversary of the "Four Weeks of Common Calamity", and Shanghai was under special martial law. Our school, from 2:00 PM to after 5:00 PM, still had no place to display, and had no choice but to bring back all the original achievements, resulting in a futile trip. This is the true situation of the day's events. Now, because colleagues, friends, and students' families have asked our school why we had the name of participating but did not see the reality of participating, we have not been able to reply to each one. We respectfully request that you use the "Letters to the Editor" column of your esteemed newspaper to publish the above-mentioned facts to clarify the truth. We are extremely hopeful. Sincerely, Shanghai Guangdong Private Primary and Secondary School.

Respectfully, I have just read a news item in the local news column of today's newspaper, "Municipal Ferry Increases Fares." Upon investigation, the Bureau has adjusted the ferry fares this time according to the actual measured distances of each pier, and re-determined them. Among them, some are higher than the current prices, and some are lower. If, as the title of your newspaper shows, it seems that there are only increases and no decreases, it is somewhat inconsistent with the facts. I am writing to inform you, hoping for your consideration. To the Editorial Department of Shen Bao, from the First Section of the Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, December 18th.

Respectfully, I have read in today's newspaper's local news column a news item about the takeover and reorganization of the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union by pharmaceutical workers. The facts are completely inconsistent, and it is very misleading to read. The details of the matter are as follows: yesterday morning at 9:30 (i.e., 9:30 AM on the 18th), unemployed members Chen Xuetang, Qi Jinxian, Fang Zheng, Kong Baogen, Dong Xingfa, etc., led a small number of unemployed and local ruffians, dozens of people, into the office of our union. Their momentum was fierce, claiming to be here to take over and reorganize, etc. They smashed the tables, chairs, and utensils, and stole documents, seals, and other items. Zhao Zhenhui, a member of the standing committee of our union, saw that the situation was not good and that there was no reason to reason. He reported to the Third Branch of the First District of the Public Security Bureau. The police were dispatched to the scene and detained Fang Zheng and others for questioning (at this time, the remaining accomplices had fled without a trace). Zhao Zhenhui, a member of the standing committee of our union, did not want to investigate further, so the director of the office released them after reprimanding them. This is the accurate account of what happened at that time. I am therefore writing to request a correction, and I ask that you publish it in the "Letters to the Editor" column to correct the record and reveal the truth. To the Chief Editor of Shen Bao, from the Shanghai Pharmaceutical Workers' Union, December 19th.

Respectfully, I have just read today's (December 19th) local news column of your esteemed newspaper, "Today's City-Wide Congress of Trade Union Representatives," which lists the "Fourth District Silk Filature Workers' Union." Upon investigation, our union was unaware of being listed as a convener of this congress of trade union representatives, and has not recently sent anyone to participate in any external activities. We are deeply afraid of misunderstandings from the outside world, so we are writing to request that your esteemed newspaper grant a correction. To the Editing Department of Shen Bao, sincerely from the Shanghai Fourth District Silk Filature Industrial Union, December 19th.

Respectfully, upon examining the "Trade Union News" column of the 16th of this month, the agenda of the 12th meeting of the board of directors of the Knitting Industry Union is completely inconsistent, does not specify the district number, and much of the content is absurd, and should be declared invalid immediately. I am writing to inform you specifically, asking you to make corrections on our behalf. I am extremely grateful. To the Great Editor, Wang Yuanqi, Standing Supervisor of the First District Knitting Industry Union, Tang Shichang and Tang Shixin, Directors of the Board, December 19th.

Respectfully, regarding the news item in the local news column of your esteemed newspaper of the 16th of this month concerning the Special District Court's wanted notice for Ma Zhichao, which mentions Director Ma Xiaojun, I am extremely surprised. Upon investigation, this case has nothing to do with Ma Xiaojun. Ma is a soldier and does not belong to the jurisdiction of the Special District Court. On that day, my lawyer appeared in court on my behalf to explain and present proof. Therefore, the details in your newspaper are completely inconsistent with the facts. I am writing to request a corresponding correction to clarify the truth and protect my reputation. To the Shen Bao, from lawyer Chen Zemin, December 18th.

Respectfully, having read the article on the fifteenth page of the fourth section of your esteemed newspaper on the sixteenth of this month, within the local news column, an article was published titled, The Special Zone Court Orders the Arrest of Ma Zhichao, etc. Within it, it stated, After the closure of the Sino-American Bank, yesterday, thirty-nine creditors of the company, including Huang Cun Seng, filed a complaint with the First Court of the Special Zone, accusing Ma Zhichao and I of jointly committing fraud. At the preliminary hearing yesterday, none of the defendants were present. The plaintiff's agent, lawyer Tang Huaiqun, earnestly requested the issuance of an arrest warrant, which was approved." Upon investigation, on the day of the hearing, I was ill and unable to get up, and I had extended an invitation to lawyer Shan Yuhua to appear in court to make a statement. Shan reported that he had learned that the plaintiff Huang Cun Seng represented thirty-nine people in filing the lawsuit, but there were no letters of entrustment, and the circumstances were bizarre. The court ordered that formal procedures be supplemented before a summons would be issued. There was no issuance of an arrest warrant. This is completely inconsistent with what your newspaper reported. Since the Sino-American lawsuit occurred, many slanderers have fabricated facts and confused the public. I do not wish to comment on their intentions at this time. I believe that since the matter involves litigation, it should await legal resolution. However, the overturning of right and wrong requires a reckoning. Therefore, I am writing to earnestly request that you make a correction to clarify the truth. This is my sincere hope. To the gentlemen of the editing department, respectfully, Li Henian, 381 Xin Da Gu Road, British Concession, October 19th.

Respectfully, regarding the news item in your newspaper of the 19th of this month regarding a dispute in the City Chamber of Commerce, which states that Chen Zhiying, Liu Musu, and Sun Choucheng went one after another to notify the staff of the Chamber of Commerce and explain the reasons for the takeover, I am very surprised to read it. Upon investigation, on that day, Choucheng wanted to inquire about the wholesale price of Snow Flower Cream, a small product from Chinese and Western pharmacies, from Sun Feijun, a staff member of the Finance Section of the Chamber of Commerce, so he sent the articles of association. On the second floor, he met Xu Qianlin, who had a letter requesting the Chamber of Commerce to certify the goods. He wanted to accompany him to the Document Department to explain the situation, so he went with Xu to the Document Department. Shortly after, Liu Musu arrived and announced the reasons for the takeover in public. The Public Security Bureau immediately sent patrols to the meeting to maintain order and prevent people from entering or leaving. Therefore, Choucheng did not return until after 4:00 PM. The newspaper reporter saw Choucheng also at the Chamber of Commerce that day and mistakenly thought that he was there for the takeover, which led to this misreporting. I am writing to request a correction to clarify the facts. This is my sincere hope. To the Chief Editor, from Sun Choucheng.
